<tr style="font-size:85%;" class="mergedbottomrow">

<td colspan="2" style="padding-left:0;">Excluding Mayotte.</td>

<p>The <b>Comoros</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="noexcerpt"><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/39/En-us-Comoros.ogg" title="Listen"><img alt="Listen" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/11px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/17px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Speakerlink-new.svg/22px-Speakerlink-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="11" data-file-height="11" /></a><sup><span style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; padding: 0 .1em;" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Comoros.ogg" title="File:En-us-Comoros.ogg">i</a></span></sup></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'k' in 'kind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">k</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɒ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'m' in 'my'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">m</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ər/ 'er' in 'finger'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ər</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'bode'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">oʊ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'z' in 'Zion'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">z</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar">جزر القمر</span>‎, <i><span title="DIN 31635 Arabic" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">Juzur al-Qumur&#160;/ Qamar</span></i>), officially the <b>Union of the Comoros</b> (<a href="/wiki/Comorian_language" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a>: <i>Udzima wa Komori,</i> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>Union des Comores</i></span>, <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar">الاتحاد القمري</span>‎ <i><span title="DIN 31635 Arabic" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none">al-Ittiḥād al-Qumurī&#160;/ Qamarī</span></i>), is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign</a> <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_nation" title="Island nation" class="mw-redirect">island nation</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Ocean</a> located at the northern end of the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a> off the eastern coast of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> between northeastern <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and northwestern <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. Other countries near the Comoros are <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a> to the northwest and the <a href="/wiki/Seychelles" title="Seychelles">Seychelles</a> to the northeast. Its capital is <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, on <a href="/wiki/Grande_Comore" title="Grande Comore">Grande Comore</a>.</p>
<p>At 1,862&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (719&#160;sq&#160;mi), excluding the contested island of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> the Comoros is the third-smallest African nation by area. The population, excluding Mayotte, is estimated at 798,000. As a nation formed at a crossroads of many civilizations, the archipelago is noted for its diverse culture and history. The Union of the Comoros has three official languages –&#160;Comorian, Arabic and French&#160;– though French is the sole official language on Mayotte.</p>
<p>Officially, in addition to many smaller islands, the country consists of the four major islands in the <a href="/wiki/Volcanic_island" title="Volcanic island" class="mw-redirect">volcanic</a> <a href="/wiki/Comoros_Islands" title="Comoros Islands" class="mw-redirect">Comoros archipelago</a>: northwesternmost <a href="/wiki/Grande_Comore" title="Grande Comore">Grande Comore</a> (Ngazidja); <a href="/wiki/Moh%C3%A9li" title="Mohéli">Mohéli</a> (Mwali); <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Anjouan</a> (Nzwani); and southeasternmost Mayotte (Maore). Mayotte, however, has never been administered by an independent Comoros government and continues to be administered by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (currently as an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" title="Overseas department">overseas department</a>) as it was the only island in the archipelago that voted against independence in 1974. France has since <a href="/wiki/Veto" title="Veto">vetoed</a> <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> resolutions that would affirm Comorian <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereignty</a> over the island.<sup id="cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-GlobalPolicy_SC-Vetoes_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GlobalPolicy_SC-Vetoes-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-article33_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-article33-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> on the question of Mayotte becoming an overseas department of France in 2011 was held on 29 March 2009 and passed overwhelmingly.</p>
<p>The Comoros is the only state to be a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francophonie" title="Francophonie" class="mw-redirect">Francophonie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a> (of which it is the southernmost state, being the only member of the Arab League which is entirely within the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>) and the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> in 1975, the country has experienced numerous <i><a href="/wiki/Coups_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coups d'état" class="mw-redirect">coups d'état</a></i> and as of 2008<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> about half the population lives below the <a href="/wiki/International_poverty_line" title="International poverty line" class="mw-redirect">international poverty line</a> of US$1.25 a day.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The name "Comoros" derives from the Arabic word <span title="Arabic transliteration" class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none"><big>قمر</big> <i>qamar</i></span> ("<a href="/wiki/Moon" title="Moon">moon</a>").<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Comoros" title="History of Comoros">History of Comoros</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Precolonial_peoples">Precolonial peoples</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Precolonial peoples">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dhow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dhow.jpg/250px-Dhow.jpg" width="250" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dhow.jpg/375px-Dhow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Dhow.jpg/500px-Dhow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dhow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A large <a href="/wiki/Dhow" title="Dhow">dhow</a> with <a href="/wiki/Lateen" title="Lateen">lateen</a> sail rigs.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/200px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" width="200" height="300" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/300px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg/400px-Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1728" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vanilla_plantation_in_wood_dsc00190.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a> plantation.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The first human inhabitants of the Comoros Islands are thought to have been Arab, African and <a href="/wiki/Austronesian" title="Austronesian" class="mw-redirect">Austronesian</a> settlers who traveled to the islands by boat. These people arrived no later than the sixth century AD, the date of the earliest known <a href="/wiki/Archaeological" title="Archaeological" class="mw-redirect">archaeological</a> site, found on <a href="/wiki/Nzwani" title="Nzwani" class="mw-redirect">Nzwani</a>, although settlement beginning as early as the first century has been postulated.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The islands of Comoros were populated by a succession of peoples from the coast of Africa, the Arabian Peninsula and the <a href="/wiki/Persian_Gulf" title="Persian Gulf">Persian Gulf</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Malay_Archipelago" title="Malay Archipelago">Malay Archipelago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>. <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking settlers reached the islands as a part of the greater <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu expansion</a> that took place in Africa throughout the first millennium.</p>
<p>According to pre-Islamic mythology, a jinni (spirit) dropped a <a href="/wiki/Gemstone" title="Gemstone">jewel</a>, which formed a great circular inferno. This became the <a href="/wiki/Mount_Karthala" title="Mount Karthala">Karthala volcano</a>, which created the island of Comoros.</p>
<p>Development of the Comoros was divided into phases. The earliest reliably recorded phase is the Dembeni phase (ninth to tenth centuries), during which each island maintained a single, central village.<sup id="cite_ref-spear_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spear-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> From the eleventh to the fifteenth centuries, trade with the island of Madagascar and merchants from the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> flourished, smaller villages emerged, and existing towns expanded. Many Comorians can trace their genealogies to ancestors from Yemen, mainly <a href="/wiki/Hadramawt" title="Hadramawt" class="mw-redirect">Hadramawt</a>, and Oman.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Comoros">Medieval Comoros</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Medieval Comoros">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to legend,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words" class="mw-redirect"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (September 2014)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> in 632, upon hearing of <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>, islanders are said to have dispatched an emissary, Mtswa-Mwindza,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> to <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>—but by the time he arrived there, the Islamic prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> had died. Nonetheless, after a stay in Mecca, he returned to Ngazidja and led the gradual conversion of his islanders to Islam.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Among the earliest accounts of East Africa, the works of Al-Masudi describe early Islamic trade routes, and how the coast and islands were frequently visited by <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> including <a href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia" class="mw-redirect">Persian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arab" title="Arab" class="mw-redirect">Arab</a> merchants and sailors in search of <a href="/wiki/Coral" title="Coral">coral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ambergris" title="Ambergris">ambergris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tortoiseshell" title="Tortoiseshell">tortoiseshell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> and slaves. They also brought Islam to the people of the <a href="/wiki/Zanj" title="Zanj">Zanj</a> including Comoros. As the importance of Comoros grew along the East African coast, both small and large <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosques</a> were constructed. Despite its distance from the coast, Comoros is situated along the <i>Swahili Coast</i> in <a href="/wiki/East_Africa" title="East Africa">East Africa</a>. It was a major hub of trade and an important location in a network of trading towns that included <a href="/wiki/Kilwa_Kisiwani" title="Kilwa Kisiwani">Kilwa</a>, in present-day Tanzania, Sofala (an outlet for <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwean</a> gold), in <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-spear_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spear-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>After the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portuguese</a> and the collapse of East African sultanates, the powerful Omani Sultan <a href="/wiki/Saif_bin_Sultan" title="Saif bin Sultan">Saif bin Sultan</a> began to defeat the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Dutch</a> and the Portuguese. His successor <a href="/wiki/Said_bin_Sultan,_Sultan_of_Muscat_and_Oman" title="Said bin Sultan, Sultan of Muscat and Oman">Said bin Sultan</a> increased Omani Arab influence in region, moving his administration to nearby <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>, which came under <a href="/wiki/Oman" title="Oman">Omani</a> rule. Nevertheless, the Comoros remained independent, and although the three smaller islands were usually politically unified, the largest island, Ngazidja, was divided into a number of autonomous kingdome (<i>ntsi</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_Spear_1984_291.E2.80.93305_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Spear_1984_291.E2.80.93305-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>By the time Europeans showed interest in the Comoros, the islanders were well placed to take advantage of their needs, initially supplying ships of the route to India and, later, slaves to the plantation islands in the <a href="/wiki/Mascarenes" title="Mascarenes" class="mw-redirect">Mascarenes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_Spear_1984_291.E2.80.93305_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas_Spear_1984_291.E2.80.93305-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="European_contact_and_French_colonization">European contact and French colonization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: European contact and French colonization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Camora.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Camora.jpg/250px-Camora.jpg" width="250" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b4/Camora.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b4/Camora.jpg 2x" data-file-width="341" data-file-height="234" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Camora.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An 1808 map refers to the islands as "Camora".</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Franz_Sikora_038.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Franz_Sikora_038.jpg/220px-Franz_Sikora_038.jpg" width="220" height="306" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Franz_Sikora_038.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Franz_Sikora_038.jpg 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="440" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Franz_Sikora_038.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sultan Said Ali bin Said Omar of Grande Comore (1897)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Portuguese explorers first visited the <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a> in 1505 and the islands provided provisions to the Portuguese fort at Mozambique throughout the 16th century.</p>
<p>In 1793, Malagasy warriors from Madagascar first started raiding the islands for <a href="/wiki/Slave" title="Slave" class="mw-redirect">slaves</a>. On Comoros, it was estimated in 1865 that as much as 40% of the population consisted of slaves.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> France first established <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">colonial</a> rule in the Comoros in 1841. The first French colonists landed in Mayotte, and Andrian Tsouli, the Malagasy King of Mayotte, signed the Treaty of April 1841, which ceded the island to the French authorities.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Comoros served as a way station for merchants sailing to the Far East and India until the opening of the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> significantly reduced traffic passing through the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a>. The native commodities exported by the Comoros were <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconuts</a>, cattle and tortoiseshell. French settlers, French-owned companies, and wealthy Arab merchants established a plantation-based economy that used about one-third of the land for export crops. After its annexation, France converted Mayotte into a sugar plantation colony. The other islands were soon transformed as well, and the major crops of <a href="/wiki/Ylang-ylang" title="Ylang-ylang" class="mw-redirect">ylang-ylang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coffee" title="Coffee">coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa bean</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sisal" title="Sisal">sisal</a> were introduced.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 1886, Mohéli was placed under French protection by its Sultan Mardjani Abdou Cheikh. That same year, despite having no authority to do so, Sultan Said Ali of Bambao, one of the sultanates on Ngazidja, placed the island under French protection in exchange for French support of his claim to the entire island, which he retained until his abdication in 1910. In 1908 The islands were unified under a single administration (<i>Colonie de Mayotte et Dépendances</i>) and placed under the authority of the French colonial governor general of Madagascar. In 1909, Sultan Said Muhamed of Anjouan abdicated in favor of French rule. In 1912 the colony and the protectorates were abolished and the islands became a province of the colony of Madagascar.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Agreement was reached with France in 1973 for Comoros to become independent in 1978. The deputies of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> abstained. Referendums were held on all four of the islands. Three voted for independence by large margins, while Mayotte voted against, and remains under French administration. On 6 July 1975, however, the Comorian parliament passed a unilateral resolution declaring independence. Ahmed Abdallah proclaimed the independence of the Comorian State (<i>État comorien</i>; دولة القمر) and became its first president.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_.281975.29">Independence (1975)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Independence (1975)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The next 30 years were a period of political turmoil. On 3 August 1975, president <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Abdallah" title="Ahmed Abdallah">Ahmed Abdallah</a> was removed from office in an armed coup and replaced with United National Front of the Comoros (UNF) member Prince <a href="/wiki/Said_Mohammed_Jaffar" title="Said Mohammed Jaffar" class="mw-redirect">Said Mohammed Jaffar</a>. Months later, in January 1976, Jaffar was ousted in favor of his Minister of Defense <a href="/wiki/Ali_Soilih" title="Ali Soilih">Ali Soilih</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Mukonoweshuro:555-577_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mukonoweshuro:555-577-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>At this time, the population of Mayotte voted against independence from France in two referenda. The <a href="/wiki/Comorian_independence_referendum,_1974" title="Comorian independence referendum, 1974">first</a>, held in December 1974, won 63.8% support for maintaining ties with France, while the <a href="/wiki/Mahoran_status_referendum,_1976" title="Mahoran status referendum, 1976">second</a>, held in February 1976, confirmed that vote with an overwhelming 99.4%. The three remaining islands, ruled by President Soilih, instituted a number of <a href="/wiki/Socialism" title="Socialism">socialist</a> and isolationist policies that soon strained relations with France. On 13 May 1978, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Denard" title="Bob Denard">Bob Denard</a> returned to overthrow President Soilih and reinstate Abdallah with the support of the French, Rhodesian and South African governments. During Soilih's brief rule, he faced seven additional coup attempts until he was finally forced from office and killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Mukonoweshuro:555-577_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mukonoweshuro:555-577-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In contrast to Soilih, Abdallah's presidency was marked by authoritarian rule and increased adherence to traditional Islam<sup id="cite_ref-Bakar:181-191_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakar:181-191-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and the country was renamed the Federal <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Republic" title="Islamic Republic" class="mw-redirect">Islamic Republic</a> of Comoros (<i>République Fédérale Islamique des Comores</i>; جمهورية القمر الإتحادية الإسلامية ). Abdallah continued as president until 1989 when, fearing a probable <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a>, he signed a decree ordering the Presidential Guard, led by Bob Denard, to disarm the armed forces. Shortly after the signing of the decree, Abdallah was allegedly shot dead in his office by a disgruntled military officer, though later sources claim an antitank missile was launched into his bedroom and killed him.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Although Denard was also injured, it is suspected that Abdallah's killer was a soldier under his command.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A few days later, Bob Denard was evacuated to South Africa by French paratroopers. Said Mohamed Djohar, Soilih's older half-brother, then became president, and served until September 1995, when Bob Denard returned and attempted another coup. This time France intervened with paratroopers and forced Denard to surrender.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The French removed Djohar to Reunion, and the Paris-backed <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Taki_Abdulkarim" title="Mohamed Taki Abdulkarim" class="mw-redirect">Mohamed Taki Abdulkarim</a> became president by election. He led the country from 1996, during a time of labor crises, government suppression, and secessionist conflicts, until his death November 1998. He was succeeded by Interim President <a href="/wiki/Tadjidine_Ben_Said_Massounde" title="Tadjidine Ben Said Massounde">Tadjidine Ben Said Massounde</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The islands of <a href="/wiki/Anjouan" title="Anjouan">Anjouan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moh%C3%A9li" title="Mohéli">Mohéli</a> declared their independence from the Comoros in 1997, in an attempt to restore French rule. But France rejected their request, leading to bloody confrontations between federal troops and rebels.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In April 1999, Colonel <a href="/wiki/Azali_Assoumani" title="Azali Assoumani">Azali Assoumani</a>, Army Chief of Staff, seized power in a bloodless coup, overthrowing the Interim President Massounde, citing weak leadership in the face of the crisis. This was the Comoros' 18th coup, or attempted <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup d'état</a> since independence in 1975.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Azali failed to consolidate power and reestablish control over the islands, which was the subject of international criticism. The <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, under the auspices of President <a href="/wiki/Thabo_Mbeki" title="Thabo Mbeki">Thabo Mbeki</a> of South Africa, imposed sanctions on Anjouan to help broker negotiations and effect reconciliation.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> The official name of the country was changed to the Union of the Comoros and a new system of political autonomy was instituted for each island, plus a union government for the three islands was added.</p>
<p>Azali stepped down in 2002 to run in the democratic election of the President of the Comoros, which he won. Under ongoing international pressure, as a military ruler who had originally come to power by force, and was not always democratic while in office, Azali led the Comoros through constitutional changes that enabled new elections.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> A <i>Loi des compétences</i> law was passed in early 2005 that defines the responsibilities of each governmental body, and is in the process of implementation. The elections in 2006 were won by <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Abdallah_Mohamed_Sambi" title="Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi">Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi</a>, a Sunni Muslim cleric nicknamed the "Ayatollah" for his time spent studying Islam in Iran. Azali honored the election results, thus allowing the first peaceful and democratic exchange of power for the archipelago.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Colonel <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_Bacar" title="Mohammed Bacar" class="mw-redirect">Mohammed Bacar</a>, a French-trained former gendarme, seized power as President in Anjouan in 2001. He staged a vote in June 2007 to confirm his leadership that was rejected as illegal by the Comoros federal government and the African Union. On 25 March 2008 hundreds of soldiers from the African Union and Comoros seized rebel-held Anjouan, generally welcomed by the population: there have been reports of hundreds, if not thousands, of people tortured during Bacar's tenure.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Some rebels were killed and injured, but there are no official figures. At least 11 civilians were wounded. Some officials were imprisoned. Bacar fled in a speedboat to the French Indian Ocean territory of Mayotte to seek asylum. Anti-French protests followed in Comoros (see <a href="/wiki/2008_invasion_of_Anjouan" title="2008 invasion of Anjouan">2008 invasion of Anjouan</a>).</p>
<p>Since independence from France, the Comoros experienced more than 20 coups or attempted coups.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Following elections in late 2010, former Vice-President <a href="/wiki/Ikililou_Dhoinine" title="Ikililou Dhoinine">Ikililou Dhoinine</a> was inaugurated as President on 26 May 2011. A member of the ruling party, Dhoinine was supported in the election by the incumbent President Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi. Dhoinine, a pharmacist by training, is the first President of Comoros from the island of Mohéli.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Comoros" title="Geography of Comoros">Geography of Comoros</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cn-map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e3/Cn-map.png" width="330" height="355" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="330" data-file-height="355" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cn-map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A map of Comoros.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Comoros is formed by <a href="/wiki/Ngazidja" title="Ngazidja" class="mw-redirect">Ngazidja</a> (Grande Comore), <a href="/wiki/Mwali" title="Mwali" class="mw-redirect">Mwali</a> (Mohéli), and <a href="/wiki/Nzwani" title="Nzwani" class="mw-redirect">Nzwani</a> (Anjouan), three major islands in the Comoros Archipelago, as well as many minor islets. The islands are officially known by their Comorian language names, though international sources still use their French names (given in parentheses above). The capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, is located on Ngazidja. The archipelago is situated in the Indian Ocean, in the <a href="/wiki/Mozambique_Channel" title="Mozambique Channel">Mozambique Channel</a>, between the African coast (nearest to <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">Mozambique</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a>, with no land borders.</p>
<p>At 2,034&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (785&#160;sq&#160;mi), it is one of the smallest countries in the world. The Comoros also has claim to 320&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (120&#160;sq&#160;mi) of territorial seas. The interiors of the islands vary from steep mountains to low hills.</p>
<p>Ngazidja is the largest of the Comoros Archipelago, approximately equal in area to the other islands combined. It is also the most recent island, and therefore has rocky soil. The island's two volcanoes, <a href="/wiki/Karthala" title="Karthala" class="mw-redirect">Karthala</a> (active) and <a href="/wiki/La_Grille" title="La Grille">La Grille</a> (dormant), and the lack of good harbors are distinctive characteristics of its terrain. Mwali, with its capital at <a href="/wiki/Fomboni" title="Fomboni">Fomboni</a>, is the smallest of the four major islands. Nzwani, whose capital is <a href="/wiki/Mutsamudu" title="Mutsamudu">Mutsamudu</a>, has a distinctive triangular shape caused by three mountain chains, Sima, Nioumakele, and Jimilime, emanating from a central peak, Ntringi (1,575&#160;m or 5,167&#160;ft).</p>
<p>The islands of the Comoros Archipelago were formed by volcanic activity. <a href="/wiki/Mount_Karthala" title="Mount Karthala">Mount Karthala</a>, an active <a href="/wiki/Shield_volcano" title="Shield volcano">shield volcano</a> located on Ngazidja, is the country's highest point, at 2,361&#160;m or 7,748&#160;ft (2,362&#160;m) It contains the Comoros' largest patch of its disappearing rainforest. Karthala is currently one of the most active volcanoes in the world, with a minor eruption in May 2006, and prior eruptions as recently as April 2005 and 1991. In the 2005 eruption, which lasted from 17 to 19 April, 40,000 citizens were evacuated, and the <a href="/wiki/Crater_lake" title="Crater lake">crater lake</a> in the volcano's 3 by 4&#160;km (1.9 by 2.5&#160;mi) caldera was destroyed.</p>
<p>The Comoros also lays claim to the <a href="/wiki/Glorioso_Islands" title="Glorioso Islands">Glorioso Islands</a>, comprising Grande Glorieuse, Île du Lys, Wreck Rock, South Rock, Verte Rocks (three islets), and three unnamed islets, one of France's <i><a href="/wiki/Scattered_islands_in_the_Indian_Ocean" title="Scattered islands in the Indian Ocean" class="mw-redirect">Îles Éparses or Îles éparses de l'océan indien</a></i> (Scattered islands in the Indian Ocean) possessions. The Glorioso Islands were administered by the colonial Comoros before 1975, and are therefore sometimes considered part of the Comoros Archipelago. <a href="/wiki/Banc_du_Geyser" title="Banc du Geyser">Banc du Geyser</a>, a former island in the Comoros Archipelago, now submerged, is geographically located in the <i>Îles Éparses</i>, but was annexed by Madagascar in 1976 as an unclaimed territory. The Comoros now claims it as part of its exclusive economic zone.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The climate is generally tropical and mild, and the two major seasons are distinguishable by their relative raininess. The temperature reaches an average of 29–30&#160;°C (84–86&#160;°F) in March, the hottest month in the rainy season (called kashkazi, December to April), and an average low of 19&#160;°C (66&#160;°F) in the cool, dry season (kusi, May to November).<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The islands are rarely subject to cyclones.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology_and_environment">Ecology and environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Ecology and environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Comoros constitute an <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> in their own right, <a href="/wiki/Comoros_forests" title="Comoros forests">Comoros forests</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Comoros" title="Politics of Comoros" class="mw-redirect">Politics of Comoros</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/300px-Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" width="300" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/450px-Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/600px-Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="469" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Capital_of_the_Comores_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, capital of the Comoros, with Harbor Bay and Central Mosque.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Politics of the Comoros takes place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Federation" title="Federation">federal</a> <a href="/wiki/Presidential_system" title="Presidential system">presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Comoros" title="President of the Comoros" class="mw-redirect">President of the Comoros</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. The Constitution of the Union of the Comoros was ratified by referendum on 23 December 2001, and the islands' constitutions and executives were elected in the following months. It had previously been considered a military dictatorship, and the transfer of power from Azali Assoumani to Ahmed Abdallah Mohamed Sambi in May 2006 was the first peaceful transfer in Comorian history.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power" class="mw-redirect">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. Federal <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power" class="mw-redirect">legislative power</a> is vested in both the <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a> and parliament. The preamble of the constitution guarantees an Islamic inspiration in governance, a commitment to human rights, and several specific enumerated rights, democracy, "a common destiny" for all Comorians. Each of the islands (according to Title II of the Constitution) has a great amount of autonomy in the Union, including having their own constitutions (or Fundamental Law), president, and Parliament. The presidency and Assembly of the Union are distinct from each of the Islands' governments. The presidency of the Union rotates between the islands.<sup id="cite_ref-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Mohéli holds the current presidency rotation, and so Ikililou Dhoinine is President of the Union; Grand Comore and Anjouan follow in four-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_system">Legal system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legal system">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Comorian <a href="/wiki/Legal_system" title="Legal system" class="mw-redirect">legal system</a> rests on <a href="/wiki/Islamic#Law" title="Islamic" class="mw-redirect">Islamic law</a>, an inherited French (<a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Code" title="Napoleonic Code">Napoleonic Code</a>) legal code, and customary law (mila na ntsi). Village elders, kadis or civilian courts settle most disputes. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative" title="Legislative" class="mw-redirect">legislative</a> and the executive. The Supreme Court acts as a Constitutional Council in resolving constitutional questions and supervising presidential elections. As High Court of Justice, the Supreme Court also arbitrates in cases where the government is accused of malpractice. The Supreme Court consists of two members selected by the president, two elected by the Federal Assembly, and one by the council of each island.<sup id="cite_ref-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CfHR_Law-of-the-Union-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_culture">Political culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Political culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Around 80 percent of the central government's annual budget is spent on the country's complex electoral system which provides for a semi-autonomous government and president for each of the three islands and a rotating presidency for the overarching Union government.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> A referendum took place on 16 May 2009 to decide whether to cut down the government's unwieldy political bureaucracy. 52.7% of those eligible voted, and 93.8% of votes were cast in approval of the referendum. The referendum would cause each island's president to become a governor and the ministers to become councilors.<sup id="cite_ref-allafrica20090519_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allafrica20090519-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As of 2008, Comoros and <a href="/wiki/Mauritania" title="Mauritania">Mauritania</a> are considered by US-based organization <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a> as the only real <a href="/wiki/Electoral_democracy" title="Electoral democracy" class="mw-redirect">electoral democracies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arab_world" title="Arab world">Arab world</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Also in 2008, the Comoros were ranked 14th out of 48 sub-Saharan African countries in the <a href="/wiki/Ibrahim_Index_of_African_Governance" title="Ibrahim Index of African Governance">Ibrahim Index of African Governance</a>. The Ibrahim Index is a comprehensive measure of African governance, based on a number of different variables which reflect the success with which governments deliver essential political goods to its citizens.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Comoros" title="Foreign relations of Comoros" class="mw-redirect">Foreign relations of Comoros</a></div>
<p>In November 1975, Comoros became the 143rd member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. The new nation was defined as comprising the entire <a href="/wiki/Archipelago" title="Archipelago">archipelago</a>, although France continues to maintain control over the island of <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a> as an <a href="/wiki/Overseas_department" title="Overseas department">overseas department</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Comoros has repeatedly pressed its claim to Mayotte before the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>, which adopted a series of resolutions under the caption "Question of the Comorian Island of Mayotte", opining that Mayotte belongs to Comoros under the principle that the territorial integrity of colonial territories should be preserved upon independence. As a practical matter, however, these resolutions have little effect and there is no foreseeable likelihood that Mayotte will become <i>de facto</i> part of Comoros without its people's consent. More recently, the Assembly has maintained this item on its agenda but deferred it from year to year without taking action. Other bodies, including the UN General Assembly, the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_African_Unity" title="Organization of African Unity" class="mw-redirect">Organization of African Unity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Movement of Non-Aligned Countries</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, have similarly questioned French sovereignty over Mayotte.<sup id="cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Comoros is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Arab_League" title="Arab League">Arab League</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Development_Fund" title="European Development Fund">European Development Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a>, the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean_Commission" title="Indian Ocean Commission">Indian Ocean Commission</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_Development_Bank" title="African Development Bank">African Development Bank</a>. On 10 April 2008, Comoros became the 179th nation to accept the <a href="/wiki/Kyoto_Protocol" title="Kyoto Protocol">Kyoto Protocol</a> to the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Comoros" title="Military of Comoros">Military of Comoros</a></div>
<p>The military resources of the Comoros consist of a small standing army and a 500-member police force, as well as a 500-member defense force. A defence treaty with France provides naval resources for protection of territorial waters, training of Comorian military personnel, and air surveillance. France maintains a few senior officers presence in Comoros at government request. France maintains a small maritime base and a <a href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Legion" title="French Foreign Legion">Foreign Legion</a> Detachment (DLEM) on <a href="/wiki/Mayotte" title="Mayotte">Mayotte</a>.</p>
<p>Once the new government was installed in May–June 2011, an expert mission from UNREC (Lomé) came to Comoros and produced guidelines for the elaboration of a national security policy, which were discussed by different actors, notably the national defence authorities and civil society.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> By the end of the programme in end March 2012, a normative framework agreed upon by all entities involved in SSR will have been established. This will then have to be adopted by Parliament and implemented by the authorities.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Comoros" title="Economy of Comoros">Economy of Comoros</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/350px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" width="350" height="273" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/525px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg/700px-Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1107" data-file-height="865" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Comoros.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A proportional representation of Comoros's exports.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Comoros is one of the world's poorest countries. Economic growth and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_reduction" title="Poverty reduction">poverty reduction</a> are major priorities for the government. With a rate of 14.3%, unemployment is considered very high. <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hunting" title="Hunting">hunting</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Forestry" title="Forestry">forestry</a>, is the leading sector of the economy, and 38.4% of the working population is employed in the <a href="/wiki/Primary_sector_of_industry" title="Primary sector of industry" class="mw-redirect">primary sector</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning.2C_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning.2C_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>High population densities, as much as 1000 per square kilometer in the densest agricultural zones, for what is still a mostly rural, agricultural economy may lead to an environmental crisis in the near future, especially considering the high rate of population growth. In 2004 Comoros' real GDP growth was a low 1.9% and real GDP per capita continued to decline. These declines are explained by factors including declining investment, drops in consumption, rising inflation, and an increase in trade imbalance due in part to lowered cash crop prices, especially vanilla.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning.2C_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_the_General_Commissioner_for_Planning.2C_Ministry_of_Planning_and_Regional_Development-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Fiscal policy is constrained by erratic fiscal revenues, a bloated civil service wage bill, and an external debt that is far above the HIPC threshold. Membership in the franc zone, the main anchor of stability, has nevertheless helped contain pressures on domestic prices.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Comoros has an inadequate transportation system, a young and rapidly increasing population, and few natural resources. The low educational level of the labor force contributes to a subsistence level of economic activity, high <a href="/wiki/Unemployment" title="Unemployment">unemployment</a>, and a heavy dependence on foreign grants and technical assistance. Agriculture contributes 40% to <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">GDP</a>, employs 80% of the labor force, and provides most of the exports. Comoros is the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Ylang-ylang" title="Ylang-ylang" class="mw-redirect">ylang-ylang</a>, and a large producer of <a href="/wiki/Vanilla" title="Vanilla">vanilla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The government is struggling to upgrade education and technical training, to privatize commercial and industrial enterprises, to improve health services, to diversify exports, to promote tourism, and to reduce the high population growth rate.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Comoros claims the <a href="/wiki/Banc_du_Geyser" title="Banc du Geyser">Banc du Geyser</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Glorioso_Islands" title="Glorioso Islands">Glorioso Islands</a> as part of its exclusive economic zone.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Comoros is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (<a href="/wiki/OHADA" title="OHADA">OHADA</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-ohada.com_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ohada.com-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Society">Society</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Society">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Comoros" title="Demographics of Comoros">Demographics of Comoros</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/220px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" width="220" height="301" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/330px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg/440px-Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="812" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moroni_Mosque_Photo_by_Sascha_Grabow.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Moroni Mosque</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With fewer than a million people, the Comoros is one of the least populous countries in the world, but is also one of the most densely populated, with an average of 275 inhabitants per square kilometre (710/sq&#160;mi). In 2001, 34% of the population was considered urban, but that is expected to grow, since rural population growth is negative, while overall population growth is still relatively high.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Almost half the population of Comoros is under the age of 15.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Major urban centers include <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mutsamudu" title="Mutsamudu">Mutsamudu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Domoni" title="Domoni">Domoni</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fomboni" title="Fomboni">Fomboni</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ts%C3%A9mb%C3%A9hou" title="Tsémbéhou" class="mw-redirect">Tsémbéhou</a>. There are between 200,000 and 350,000 Comorians in France.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The islands of the Comoros share mostly African-Arab origins. <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_people" title="Malagasy people">Malagasy</a> (Christian) and <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_Groups_of_South_Asia" title="Ethnic Groups of South Asia" class="mw-redirect">Indian</a> (mostly <a href="/wiki/Ismaili" title="Ismaili" class="mw-redirect">Ismaili</a>) minorities also exist, as well as minorities mostly descended from early French settlers. <a href="/wiki/Chinese_people" title="Chinese people">Chinese people</a> are also present on Mayotte and parts of Grande Comore (especially Moroni). A small <a href="/wiki/White_African" title="White African" class="mw-redirect">white minority</a> of <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> with other European (i.e. Dutch, British and Portuguese) ancestry lives in Comoros. Most French left after independence in 1975.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Comoros" title="Languages of the Comoros">Languages of the Comoros</a></div>
<p>The most common <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Comoros" title="Languages of the Comoros">language in Comoros</a> is <a href="/wiki/Comorian_language" title="Comorian language">Comorian</a>, or <i>Shikomor</i>. It is a language related to <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> although with less Arabic influence than Swahili, with four different variants (Shingazidja, Shimwali, Shinzwani, and Shimaore) being spoken on each of the four islands. No <a href="/wiki/Official_script" title="Official script">official alphabet</a> existed in 1992, but <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin</a> scripts are both used.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue_report_for_Comoros_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue_report_for_Comoros-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>French and <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a> are also official languages, along with Comorian. Arabic is widely known as a second language, being the language of Quranic teaching. French is the administrative language and the language of all non-Quranic formal education. A <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bushi_language" title="Bushi language">Kibushi</a>, is spoken by approximately a third of the population of Mayotte.<sup id="cite_ref-Ethnologue_report_for_Comoros_53-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ethnologue_report_for_Comoros-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Comoros" title="Religion in Comoros">Religion in Comoros</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Sunni_Islam" title="Sunni Islam">Sunni Islam</a> is <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Comoros" title="Islam in Comoros">the dominant religion</a>, representing as much as 98% of the population. <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Comoros" title="Roman Catholicism in Comoros">A minority of the population</a> of Mayotte, mostly immigrants from metropolitan France, are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Comoros" title="Health in Comoros">Health in Comoros</a></div>
<p>There are 15 physicians per 100,000 people. The <a href="/wiki/Fertility_rate" title="Fertility rate" class="mw-redirect">fertility rate</a> was 4.7 per adult woman in 2004. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth is 67 for females and 62 for males.<sup id="cite_ref-afro.who.int_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afro.who.int-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Comoros" title="Education in Comoros">Education in Comoros</a></div>
<p>Almost all of the educated populace of the Comoros have attended <a href="/wiki/Quranic_school" title="Quranic school" class="mw-redirect">Quranic schools</a> at some point in their lives, often before regular schooling. Here, boys and girls are taught about the <a href="/wiki/Qur%27an" title="Qur'an" class="mw-redirect">Qur'an</a>, and memorize it. Some parents specifically choose this early schooling to offset French schools children usually attend later. Since independence and the ejection of French teachers, the education system has been plagued by poor teacher training and poor results, though recent stability may allow for substantial improvements.<sup id="cite_ref-Bakar:181-191_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bakar:181-191-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, 44.2% of children ages 5 to 14 years were attending school. There is a general lack of facilities, equipment, qualified teachers, textbooks and other resources. <a href="/wiki/Salaries" title="Salaries" class="mw-redirect">Salaries</a> for teachers are often so far in arrears that many refuse to work.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>About fifty-seven percent of the population is literate in the <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">Latin script</a> while more than 90% are literate in the <a href="/wiki/Arabic_script" title="Arabic script">Arabic script</a>; total literacy is incorrectly estimated at 62.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Comorian has no native script, but both Arabic and Latin scripts are used.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Holidays_in_Comoros" title="Holidays in Comoros" class="mw-redirect">Holidays in Comoros</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Kinship_and_social_structure">Kinship and social structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Kinship and social structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Comorian society is matrilineal and inheritance is passed from mothers to daughters, similar to <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Malayo-Polynesians</a> who are matrilineal (<a href="/wiki/Minangkabau_people" title="Minangkabau people">Minangkabau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cham_people" title="Cham people">Cham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rade_people" title="Rade people">Rade</a>, <a href="/wiki/Moken_people" title="Moken people">Moken</a>). Like in matrilineal Malayo-Polynesian societies, the dominant power of the society belongs to men.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Comoro_Islands" title="Music of the Comoro Islands">Music of the Comoro Islands</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Taarab" title="Taarab">taarab</a> music remains the most influential genre on the islands, and a Comorian version called <i>twarab</i> is popular.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Comoros&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Comoros" title="Media of Comoros">Media of Comoros</a></div>
<p>There is a government-owned national <a href="/wiki/Newspaper" title="Newspaper">newspaper</a> in Comoros, <a href="/wiki/Al-Watwan" title="Al-Watwan">Al-Watwan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> published in <a href="/wiki/Moroni,_Comoros" title="Moroni, Comoros">Moroni</a>. Radio Comoros is the national radio service and Comoros National TV is the television service.</p>

<li id="cite_note-GA31_first-resolution-6"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_6-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-GA31_first-resolution_6-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The first UN General Assembly Resolution regarding the matter, "<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20080408191407/http://un.cti.depaul.edu/Countries/Comoros/1156213396.pdf">Question of the Comorian island of Mayotte</a> (PDF)", United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/31/4, (21 October 1976) states "the occupation by France of the Comorian island of Mayotte constitutes a flagrant encroachment on the national unity of the Comorian State, a Member of the United Nations," rejecting the French-administered referendums and condemning French presence in Mayotte.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As defined by the <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_African_Unity" title="Organization of African Unity" class="mw-redirect">Organization of African Unity</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">Movement of Non-Aligned Countries</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Organisation_of_Islamic_Cooperation" title="Organisation of Islamic Cooperation">Organisation of Islamic Cooperation</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_General_Assembly" title="United Nations General Assembly">United Nations General Assembly</a>: the most recent UN General Assembly Resolution regarding the matter, "Question of the Comorian island of Mayotte," United Nations General Assembly Resolution A/RES/49/18, (6 December 1994) states "the results of the referendum of 22 December 1974 were to be considered on a global basis and not island by island,...Reaffirms the sovereignty of the Islamic Federal Republic of the Comoros over the island of Mayotte". <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20080106080523/http://un.cti.depaul.edu/public/Comoros/10/English/">Several resolutions expressing similar sentiments were passed between 1977 (31/4) and 1994 (49/18).</a></span></li>
